### Post by LaRoza on 2008-10-31
Rules:
[LIST]
[*] **Forum guidelines on content apply. In other words, safe for kids and safe for work. If you have doubts about the images appropriateness, please don't post it (some people are at work or are uncomfortable with some images). The easiest way to cover up minor things would be to put an open window in front of it.**
[*] Try not to quote embedded images; take a moment to snip them out.
[*] Off-topic posts will be edited or moved.
[*] **Thumbnail your image, or use the forum's attachment system. Full-size embedded images are annoying and will be snipped mercilessly.**
[*] Take a moment and tell everyone the details of your desktop, such as the theme name, the wallpaper name, the icons and any programs you're using in the image.
[/LIST]
:) :)

### Post by elmer_42 on 2008-10-31
As you can see in the lower right of the screen, it's not November here yet, that comes in 7 hours. However, in honor of Ubuntu 8.10 coming out, I tried to make a brown/earthy desktop. I had my Tint looking a lot different than it does now, but I just like it too much the way it was, so I just changed a few of the colors on it. I went through a *lot* of brown wallpapers before I found this one. If you would like the configuration files for any of my applications, just ask, I would be more than glad to post them up.

[[img]http://arch.kimag.es/resized/10056377.png[/img]](http://arch.kimag.es/share/10056377.png)
```
Distro:          Arch Linux (x86_64)
Kernel:          2.6.27-ARCH
WM:              Openbox
WM Theme:        Fawn
GTK:             Fawn
Wall:            Mystic Sunset
                 interfacelift.com
Apps:            Tint2, Conky
```

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-10-31
I never thought I'd be using GNOME, but now that I'm on Ibex, I'm using it a lot more than KDE because it more closely resembles what KDE used to be.

Okay, so I took WIIAN's MurrineGlow Red theme and I changed the colors in the Appearance dialog. I replaced the panel backgrounds with some really old kicker backgrounds I made a long time ago for KDE.

The wallpaper is the same as when I was on KDE:  [Flora Nine]("http://delta909.deviantart.com/art/Flora-Nine-90794895?moodonly=1")

The Emerald theme is a mod of my Elegent Curve theme, which I have yet to upload.

I have Cairo-dock on the side.

And finally, my icons are Hydroxygen Red.

---

### Post by vexorian on 2008-11-01
Feck why the November thread started so long ago? I was hoping to get on first page this month :).

First is my desktop, the other is my eee. Nothing important theme wise, just took clearlooks and applied a grayish tone for selected stuff, then installed the tango-installer or whatever it is called to use the gray variation. For the small one, I installed ubuntu-eee (whatever that is called now) and modded the remix launcher (by deleting some files in the folder where it finds graphics :) )

And the background... I themed my both computers on Les Luthiers, there are white variations of those available on deviant art, if you want the link or the black versions, you may ask, however I doubt you would.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-11-01
> **elmer_42 said:**
> I'm trying to find that, but it's not in my rc.xml or my menu.xml. Where is it?
It doesn't matter where it goes. Here's an example:

```

#Menu geometry
menu.border.width: 1
menu.overlap: -5

```

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-11-01
> **andrek said:**
> Wow, that looks awesome.
Would you mind sharing the secret about the fonts you have used here?

It's no secret!

The font is called Corbel (size 9), which is really similar to the non-free font Microsoft font called Calibri that I used to use in all my KDE screenshots.

Resolution: 96 dot per inch
Smoothing: Subpixel (LCDs)
Hinting: None
Subpixel Order: RGB

### Post by K.Mandla on 2008-11-02
[[img]http://xs233.xs.to/xs233/08440/icewm-arch-493.jpg.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs233&d=08440&f=icewm-arch-493.jpg)

Arch Linux, as close as I can get to the Windows 2000/Windows XP Classic theme. 

IceWM with the WinClassic2 theme off box-look.org, standard Redmond and Raleigh themes found in the Arch GTK1.2 and GTK2 engine packages, and the downloadable Bliss wallpaper found via Wikipedia. GTK1.2 version of Firefox 2 with the "LooksFamiliar" theme applied.

volwheel for the taskbar volume control, MS Core Fonts plus the Tahoma font I found ... somewhere. Xfe set to the Windows theme and the panel colors set to match the GTK theme, XMMS with the Winamp skin (gnome-look.org), Sylpheed, XChat, GPicView, Galculator, rxvt-unicode, Leafpad, EasyTag, scrot, xscreensaver set to the morph3d screensaver. 

Am I forgetting anything? ;)

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-11-02
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Well, most of my folders inside my Home directory are shortcuts anyway (as they link to actual folders inside of a separate partition), but still I can't seem to find any option to change their icon on the folder properties dialog in Thunar. Am I missing something?
Sorry, I meant .desktop files. Here is an example of documents.desktop:

```

[Desktop Entry]
Type=Link
Encoding=UTF-8
Version=1.0
Name=Documents
Icon=emblem-documents
Name[en_US]=Documents
URL=file:///home/daniel/Documents

```[IMG]http://i103.photobucket.com/albums/m128/envyouraudience/thunar-icons.png[/IMG]

The only annoying thing about this method is that it will open the directory in a new window.

### Post by voteforpedro36 on 2008-11-02
> **steveydoteu said:**
> What envrionment is that?  It looks like something in the nature of openbox/fluxbox.

Would it be possible to post your configuration files, or PM them?

It's Openbox with Tint. I've already changed the tintrc, but here's what I can remember:
```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = multi_monitor
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom center
panel_size = 1100 24
panel_margin = 15 1 
panel_padding = 9 3
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 3
panel_border_width = 0
# Next value was changed to a certain color with the 35 set to something a bit higher, but I cant remember what it was
panel_background_color = #000711 35 
panel_border_color = #000000 120

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 120
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 6
task_icon_size = 0 
task_font = sans 8
# This was some red, now it is blue
task_active_font_color = #2f4b6e 120
task_font_color = #dcdcdc 120

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 7
task_active_background_color = #3c3c3c 0
task_background_color = #454545 0
task_border_width = 0
task_border_color = #ffffff 18
task_active_border_color = #ffffff 70

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %I:%M %p
time1_font = sans 7
time2_format = %A %B %d
time2_font = sans 7
clock_font_color = #ffffff 120

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify

```

I commented what I know should be changed in order to reproduce my last one.

The OB theme is just Onyx Citrus with a couple of color changes. Here is the themerc if you want it:

```
!! Onyx-Citrus by Dana Jansens
!! inspired by "Carbon" by p0ng, and the ever so popular Vista glass look
!! edited by voteforpedro, making it moar red

!! Menu background
menu.items.bg: flat gradient vertical
menu.items.bg.color: #2c2c2c
menu.items.bg.colorTo: #3b3838
!! Menu text
menu.items.text.color: #f5f5f3
menu.items.justify: left
menu.items.disabled.text.color: #606060

!! Menu headers
menu.title.bg: raised splitvertical gradient
menu.title.bg.color: #303030
menu.title.bg.colorTo: #181818
menu.title.text.color: white
menu.title.text.justify: center

!! Selected menu item
menu.items.active.bg: raised splitvertical gradient
menu.items.active.bg.color: #d92525
menu.items.active.bg.colorTo: #bd1515
menu.items.active.text.color: #ffffff

!! Titlebar
window.active.title.bg: raised splitvertical gradient
window.active.title.bg.color: #2c2c2c
window.active.title.bg.colorTo: #2c2c2c
window.inactive.title.bg: gradient splitvertical gradient flat
window.inactive.title.bg.color: #2c2c2c
window.inactive.title.bg.colorTo: #2c2c2c

!! Titlebar text
window.label.text.justify: center
window.active.label.bg: parentrelative
window.active.label.text.color: #f2ffff
window.inactive.label.bg: parentrelative
window.inactive.label.text.color: #605849

!! Window buttons
window.*.button.*.bg: parentrelative
window.active.button.*.hover.bg: flat splitvertical gradient border
window.inactive.button.*.hover.bg: parentrelative
window.*.button.*.pressed.bg: flat splitvertical gradient border

window.active.button.*.hover.bg.color: #d92525
window.active.button.*.hover.bg.colorTo: #bd1515
window.active.button.*.hover.bg.border.color: #ab5d20

window.active.button.*.pressed.bg.color: #99663c
window.active.button.*.pressed.bg.colorTo: #99663c
window.active.button.*.pressed.image.color: #888888
window.active.button.*.pressed.bg.border.color: #683913
window.inactive.button.*.pressed.bg.color: #ffaa64
window.inactive.button.*.pressed.bg.colorTo: #ffaa64
window.inactive.button.*.pressed.image.color: #fdceb7
window.inactive.button.*.pressed.bg.border.color: #f0832c

window.active.button.*.image.color: #e0e0e0
window.active.button.disabled.image.color: #707070
window.inactive.button.*.image.color: #747474
window.inactive.button.disabled.image.color: #c0c0c0

!! Borders
window.active.border.color: #181818
window.inactive.border.color: #404040
window.inactive.title.separator.color: #eeeee6
border.width: 1
padding.width: 2
window.handle.width: 0
window.active.client.color:  #181818
window.inactive.client.color:  #CACAB6
window.client.padding.width: 1
window.client.padding.height: 1
menu.overlap: 0

!! Font shadows
menu.items.font:shadow=y:shadowtint=30

!! On-screen displays
osd.bg: gradient vertical flat
osd.bg.color: #303030
osd.bg.colorTo: #080808

```

Seriously like 2 values changed.

The GTK is Glow Fire.

And thanks cardinals_fan.

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-11-03
> **benerivo said:**
> As usual there are many dark desktops. Does anyone use a pure white one? I used to (see [here]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/preview.php?preview=2&id=76676&file1=76676-1.png&file2=76676-2.png&file3=76676-3.png&name=Lucidity+Emerald")), and i thought it was pretty good.

Mine. Attached for easy reference.

I think a lot of people use dark desktops to save their eyes during late-night computing. I went white to avoid TOO many late nights. If it's at the point when my eyes hurt looking at my monitor, it's time to go to sleep (such as right now).

Dark desktops are great at night, but SUCK during the day.

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-11-04
> **myusername said:**
> looks nice ^^ but anyways that is the EXACT ob theme i have been looking for! it'd be nicer if i could darken the gray a little though

Just open up the ol' themerc file in ~/.themes/murrina334/openbox-3/

I just switched some of the stuff near the bottom (most of it's default):

```
# Menus
menu.title.bg: Flat Gradient Vertical border
menu.title.bg.color: #999999
menu.title.bg.colorTo: #3c3c3c
menu.title.text.color: #111111
menu.title.text.justify: Center
menu.title.bg.border.color: #222222

menu.items.bg: Flat Solid
menu.items.bg.color: #cccccc
menu.items.text.color: #333333
menu.items.disabled.text.color: #c3c3c3

menu.items.active.bg: Flat Gradient Vertical
menu.items.active.bg.color: #333333
menu.items.active.bg.colorTo: #333333
menu.items.active.text.color: #cccccc
menu.items.active.disabled.text.color: #c3c3c3
```

---

### Post by Karilex on 2008-11-04
Hello I have recently embarked on a holy crusade of conversion to linux and what most people really like when they first try ubuntu/kubuntu/xubuntu ... is that they have a much greater freedom to configure their desktop theme/icons/window borders... but unfortunately they find the task a little daunting and sometimes just don't have the inspiration, so I was wondering if you could upload a screenshot of your current desktop environment with a few links on what to download to get to that result and maybe a few instructions I'm sure that would really help us less artistic folk thanks a lot for your contribution.

Oh and don't forget to mention if you are using KDE/Gnome/Xfce or other

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2008-11-04
> **Karilex said:**
> Hello I have recently embarked on a holy crusade of conversion to linux and what most people really like when they first try ubuntu/kubuntu/xubuntu ... is that they have a much greater freedom to configure their desktop theme/icons/window borders... but unfortunately they find the task a little daunting and sometimes just don't have the inspiration, so I was wondering if you could upload a screenshot of your current desktop environment with a few links on what to download to get to that result and maybe a few instructions I'm sure that would really help us less artistic folk thanks a lot for your contribution.

Oh and don't forget to mention if you are using KDE/Gnome/Xfce or other

[http://www.gnome-look.org](http://www.gnome-look.org) <- for GNOME stuff
[http://www.kde-look.org](http://www.kde-look.org) <- for KDE
[http://www.xfce-look.org](http://www.xfce-look.org) <- XFCE
[http://www.box-look.org](http://www.box-look.org) <- for flux/open/blackbox and others

These are pretty much THE sites for desktop customization with the various desktop environments, and it's almost a given that any theme names you see here will be from one of those sites. I have the GNOME and Box variants in my Speed Dial.

For wallpapers:

[http://browse.deviantart.com/customization/wallpaper/](http://browse.deviantart.com/customization/wallpaper/)
[http://www.interfacelift.com](http://www.interfacelift.com)

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-06
> **PurposeOfReason said:**
> I would if I knew how to with the gtkrc.

```
widget_class "*Gnome*Panel*" style "gnome-panel"
widget "*Gnome*Panel*" style "gnome-panel"
class "*Gnome*Panel*" style "gnome-panel"

style "gnome-panel"
{
font_name="<fontname> bold <size>"
}
```

I just modified that slightly as I assume you[']r[e] using Gnome, not Xfce.

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-11-07
> **myusername said:**
> can anyone tell me how to brighten the close/max/min buttons on an openbox theme? here is the themerc. i need the color when the button is hovered to be white and light grey when not
According to line 73 of the theme file, the image should already be white when hovered:

```

window.active.button.hover.image.color: #ffffff

```

and per line 49, the image should normally be light grey:

```

window.active.button.unpressed.image.color: #aaaaaa

```

I'm not positive, but this looks like the Elachisto333 theme which I submitted awhile back. With that theme, the images were actually blank xbm files. In order for the button images to show up, copy the following files from a theme whose buttons you like:

```
close.xbm
iconify.xbm
max.xbm
```

and paste them in 

```
~/.themes/THEME NAME/openbox-3/
```

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-11-08
I'm currently trying out a new theme and I made the switch to the newest Amarok beta. It's surprisingly flakey considering it's the third beta and there's talk of a final release soon. The dbus interface sucks. Porting my little widget made it about 10 times as complex. Amarok only returns the track's current time in milliseconds. I came up with this to convert it. I'd be interested to see if anyone has any improvements. I'm going for most compact code.
```

milTime=`qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player PositionGet`
seconds=$((milTime/1000 % 60))
[ `echo ${#seconds}` -lt 2 ] && echo $(($milTime/60000)):0$seconds ||\
echo $(($milTime/60000)):$seconds

```
[[img]http://xs433.xs.to/xs433/08456/2008-11-08-012942_1280x800_scrot556.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs433&d=08456&f=2008-11-08-012942_1280x800_scrot556.png)

---

### Post by ddnev45 on 2008-11-09
> **LaRoza said:**
> Rules:
[LIST]
[*] **Forum guidelines on content apply. In other words, safe for kids and safe for work. If you have doubts about the images appropriateness, please don't post it (some people are at work or are uncomfortable with some images). The easiest way to cover up minor things would be to put an open window in front of it.**
[*] Try not to quote embedded images; take a moment to snip them out.
[*] Off-topic posts will be edited or moved.
[*] **Thumbnail your image, or use the forum's attachment system. *[COLOR="DarkRed"]Full-size embedded images are annoying and will be snipped mercilessly.**[/COLOR]*
[*] Take a moment and tell everyone the details of your desktop, such as the theme name, the wallpaper name, the icons and any programs you're using in the image.
[/LIST]
:) :)

Worth repeating.

### Post by elmer_42 on 2008-11-09
> **dbbolton said:**
> Right, I meant ncmpcpp. As far as I can tell, it has the same colors as ncmpc.
Oh, I thought ncmpc couldn't use colors, so that confused me. Here's my ~/.ncmpcpp/config (which, I admit, is just a quick edit of the default config file):
```
####################################################
## this is example configuration file, copy it to ##
## ~/.ncmpcpp/config and set up your preferences  ##
####################################################
#
##### connection settings #####
#
## set it in order to make tag editor and renaming files work properly
#
mpd_music_dir = "/var/lib/mpd/music"
#
#mpd_connection_timeout = "5"
#
mpd_crossfade_time = "1"
#
##### delays #####
#
## delay after playlist highlighting will be disabled (0 = don't disable)
#
#playlist_disable_highlight_delay = "5"
#
## defines how long various messages are supposed to be visible
#
#message_delay_time = "4"
#
##### song format #####
##
## for song format you can use:
##
## %l - length
## %f - short filename
## %F - full filename
## %a - artist
## %t - title
## %b - album
## %y - year
## %n - track number
## %g - genre
## %c - composer
## %p - performer
## %d - disc
## %C - comment
## %r - begin right align
##
## you can also put them in { } and then it will be displayed
## only if all requested values are available and/or define alternate
## value with { }|{ } eg. {%a - %t}|{%f}
##
## text can also have different color than the main window has,
## eg. if you want length to have other color, write [.color]%t[/color]
##
## available colors:
##
## - black
## - red
## - green
## - yellow
## - blue
## - magenta
## - cyan
## - white
##
#
song_list_format = "{[.green](%n)[/green] }{[.cyan]%a[/cyan] - }{[.white]%t[/white]}|{[.blue]%l[/blue]}"
#
#song_library_format = "{%n - }{%t}|{%f}"
#
#media_library_album_format = "{(%y) }%b"
#
#tag_editor_album_format = "{(%y) }%b"
#
#browser_playlist_prefix = "[.red]playlist[/red] "
#
#selected_item_prefix = "[.magenta]"
#
#selected_item_suffix = "[/magenta]"
#
## colors are not supported for below veriables
#
#song_status_format = "{(%l) }{%a - }{%t}|{%f}"
#
#song_window_title_format = "{%a - }{%t}|{%f}"
#
##### columns settings #####
##
## syntax of song columns list format is "column column etc."
##
## - syntax for each column is:
##
## (width of column in %)[column's color]{displayed tag}
##
## - color is optional (if it's not present, default window color will be used)
##
#
#song_columns_list_format = "(8)[green]{l} (28)[cyan]{a} (28){b} (50)[red]{t}"
#
##### various settings #####
#
#playlist_display_mode = "classic" (classic/columns)
#
#incremental_seeking = "yes"
#
#seek_time = "1"
#
#autocenter_mode = "no"
#
#repeat_one_mode = "no"
#
#media_library_left_column = "a" (possible values: a,y,g,c,p, legend above)
#
#default_find_mode = "wrapped" (wrapped/normal)
#
#default_space_mode = "add" (add/select)
#
#default_tag_editor_left_col = "albums" (albums/dirs)
#
#default_tag_editor_pattern = "%n - %t"
#
#header_visibility = "yes"
#
#statusbar_visibility = "yes"
#
#fancy_scrolling = "yes"
#
#follow_now_playing_lyrics = "no"
#
#ncmpc_like_songs_adding = "no" (enabled - add/remove, disabled - always add)
#
#enable_window_title = "yes"
#
##### colors definitions #####
#
#colors_enabled = "yes"
#
#empty_tag_color = "cyan"
#
#header_window_color = "default"
#
#volume_color = "default"
#
#state_line_color = "default"
#
#state_flags_color = "default"
#
main_window_color = "green"
#
#color1 = "white"
#
#color2 = "green"
#
main_window_highlight_color = "blue"
#
#progressbar_color = "default"
#
#statusbar_color = "default"
#
#active_column_color = "red"
#
#window_border_color = "green"
#
#active_window_border = "red"
#
```
I think the part that you specifically care about is this:
```
song_list_format = "{[.green](%n)[/green] }{[.cyan]%a[/cyan] - }{[.white]%t[/white]}|{[.blue]%l[/blue]}"
```

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-11-10
> **indecisive said:**
> How did you get your Hydroxygen icons to work?  "Appearance" refuses to install it (yes, AFTER customizing it).

If the Appearance settings dialog is not installing the icon theme from the tarball (e.g. hydroxygen.tar.bz), simply extract it and move the extracted folder to /home/[COLOR="Silver"]username[/COLOR]/.icons

### Post by cardinals_fan on 2008-11-10
> **elmer_42 said:**
> I just tried dwm and it confused the fire out of me. Do you know of any good, simple guides akin to the welcome prompt wmii gives you?
For me, wmii was the most confusing 10 minutes since I tried to install Lunar (operative word: tried).

As for guides, there's the man page (below).  Otherwise, I'd be happy to answer any questions, either in a separate thread or by PM.

```
DWM(1)                                                                  DWM(1)



NAME
       dwm - dynamic window manager

SYNOPSIS
       dwm [-v]

DESCRIPTION
       dwm  is  a  dynamic  window manager for X. It manages windows in tiled,
       monocle and floating layouts. Either layout can be applied dynamically,
       optimising the environment for the application in use and the task per&#8208;
       formed.

       In tiled layouts windows are managed in a master and stacking area. The
       master  area  contains the window which currently needs most attention,
       whereas the stacking area contains all other windows. In monocle layout
       all  windows  are maximised to the screen size. In floating layout win&#8208;
       dows can be resized and moved freely. Dialog windows are always managed
       floating, regardless of the layout applied.

       Windows are grouped by tags. Each window can be tagged with one or mul&#8208;
       tiple tags. Selecting certain tags  displays  all  windows  with  these
       tags.

       dwm  contains a small status bar which displays all available tags, the
       layout, the title of the focused window, and the text read  from  stan&#8208;
       dard  input.  A floating window is indicated with an empty square and a
       maximised floating window is indicated with a filled square before  the
       windows title.  The selected tags are indicated with a different color.
       The tags of the focused window are indicated with a  filled  square  in
       the top left corner.  The tags which are applied to one or more windows
       are indicated with an empty square in the top left corner.

       dwm draws a small border around windows to indicate the focus state.

OPTIONS
       -v     prints version information to standard output, then exits.

USAGE
   Status bar
       Standard input
              is read and displayed in the status text area.

       Button1
              click on a tag label to display all windows with that tag, click
              on the layout label toggles between tiled and floating layout.

       Button3
              click  on  a  tag  label  adds/removes all windows with that tag
              to/from the view.

       Mod1-Button1
              click on a tag label applies that tag to the focused window.

       Mod1-Button3
              click on a tag label adds/removes that tag to/from  the  focused
              window.

   Keyboard commands
       Mod1-Shift-Return
              Start xterm.

       Mod1-b Toggles bar on and off.

       Mod1-t Sets tiled layout.

       Mod1-f Sets floating layout.

       Mod1-m Sets monocle layout.

       Mod1-space
              Toggles between current and previous layout.

       Mod1-j Focus next window.

       Mod1-k Focus previous window.

       Mod1-h Decrease master area size.

       Mod1-l Increase master area size.

       Mod1-Return
              Zooms/cycles  focused  window to/from master area (tiled layouts
              only).

       Mod1-Shift-c
              Close focused window.

       Mod1-Shift-space
              Toggle focused window between tiled and floating state.

       Mod1-Tab
              Toggles to the previously selected tags.

       Mod1-Shift-[1..n]
              Apply nth tag to focused window.

       Mod1-Shift-0
              Apply all tags to focused window.

       Mod1-Control-Shift-[1..n]
              Add/remove nth tag to/from focused window.

       Mod1-[1..n]
              View all windows with nth tag.

       Mod1-0 View all windows with any tag.

       Mod1-Control-[1..n]
              Add/remove all windows with nth tag to/from the view.

       Mod1-Shift-q
              Quit dwm.

   Mouse commands
       Mod1-Button1
              Move focused window while dragging. Tiled windows will  be  tog&#8208;
              gled to the floating state.

       Mod1-Button2
              Toggles focused window between floating and tiled state.

       Mod1-Button3
              Resize focused window while dragging. Tiled windows will be tog&#8208;
              gled to the floating state.

CUSTOMIZATION
       dwm is customized by creating a custom config.h and  (re)compiling  the
       source code. This keeps it fast, secure and simple.

SEE ALSO
       dmenu(1)

BUGS
       The  status  bar may display EOF when dwm has been started by an X ses&#8208;
       sion manager like xdm(1), because those close  standard  output  before
       executing dwm.

       Java  applications  which  use  the XToolkit/XAWT backend may draw grey
       windows only. The  XToolkit/XAWT  backend  breaks  ICCCM-compliance  in
       recent  JDK 1.5 and early JDK 1.6 versions, because it assumes a repar&#8208;
       enting window manager. As a workaround  you  can  use  JDK  1.4  (which
       doesn't contain the XToolkit/XAWT backend) or you can set the following
       environment  variable  (to  use  the  older  Motif  backend   instead):
       AWT_TOOLKIT=MToolkit.

       GTK  2.10.9+  versions contain a broken Save-As file dialog implementa&#8208;
       tion, which requests to reconfigure its window size in an endless loop.
       However,  its window is still respondable during this state, so you can
       simply ignore the flicker until a new GTK version appears,  which  will
       fix this bug, approximately GTK 2.10.12+ versions.



                                    dwm-5.2                             DWM(1)
```
EDIT: I just realized that I never read the whole man page </blushes>.  dwm is even better than I thought :D

### Post by Vinno on 2008-11-11
> **ad_267 said:**
> Damn I like that desktop a lot. Did you get use mpd with pulse audio or with Alsa? I'm having issues with mpd not being able to connect with pulse audio and I'm not sure what I'm doing wrong. Any tips for someone just getting started with Awesome?

With pulse, [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=4601963&postcount=3](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=4601963&postcount=3) <-- give that a go.

Yeah handy keys to remember to start off.

Windowskey + Shift + Q = quit out of awesome.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2008-11-11
> **Opeth115 said:**
> Sweet is there some sort of guide that i can follow to get started and set it up?

i didn't know a lot about it as well mate. i simply used robber's config files and changed a few attributes like the choice of the terminal, mediaplayer, fonts and such, thats all! the config file sure luks very simple and is easy to modify! i am posting his configs here to start with! the config is optimized for a 1680x1050 screen, but its pretty easy to modify though.

[http://robber49.net/files/fvwm.tar.gz]("http://robber49.net/files/fvwm.tar.gz")

extract the file (shud be .fvwm) and move .fvwm to ur home directory. login to fvwm and it shud be pretty much up! once i got this done, i went about changing some stuff! thats all! 

u can also refer this thread for some ongoing discussion about fvwm!

[http://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=58487]("http://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=58487")

hope that helps mate!:)

### Post by BOBSONATOR on 2008-11-11
I found this lovely dust mod

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-11-11
Any conky gurus want to give me a hand with this? I'm trying to find a way to make conky always be centered no matter what text it's displaying. Thanks in advance. 

[[img]http://xs433.xs.to/xs433/08462/2008-11-11-170741_1280x800_scrot892.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs433&d=08462&f=2008-11-11-170741_1280x800_scrot892.png)

.conkyrc
```

#avoid flicker                                                
double_buffer yes                                             

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys
own_window  yes                                 
own_window_transparent yes                      
own_window_type normal                          
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

#borders
draw_borders no
border_margin 1

#shades
draw_shades no

#position
gap_x 5  
gap_y 0  
alignment top_center

#behaviour
update_interval 1

#colour
default_color  8f8f8f
#default_shade_color 000000
own_window_colour 222222   

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont Segoe Semibold:pixelsize=10

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer none               
minimum_size 1280 0           

#mpd
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600     

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen
#${font Grunge:size=12}${time %a  %b  %d}${alignr -25}${time %k:%M}

#$alignc center text
TEXT
${voffset -1} Cpu: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${cpu}% ${color} Mem: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${mem} ${color}  |  ${color} Uptime: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${uptime_short}${color}  |  ${color} Down: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s ${color} ${totaldown wlan0} downloaded${color}  |  Up: ${color} ${color d0d0d0}${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s ${color} ${totalup wlan0} uploaded${color}  |  ${color}Root: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${fs_free /} ${color} Home: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${fs_free /home}${color}  |  Gmail: ${color d0d0d0}${execi 300 python ~/.scripts/gmail.py}${color}  |  Now Playing : ${color d0d0d0}${font}${exec echo `qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player GetMetadata | grep -m1 artist | cut -d : -f 2` " - " `qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player GetMetadata | grep -m1 title | cut -d : -f 2`}${color}



```

### Post by dlm4849 on 2008-11-11
Cool background and music. Not to get OT, but do you listen to Oceansize as well?

My conky is fairly similar to yours, and in my alignment I have top_middle and I am also using ${alignc) around my two lines. Mine stays centered no matter what.

EDIT: Also just noticed you have a value of 5 for your x gap. Mine is set at 0.

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-11-11
> **dlm4849 said:**
> Cool background and music. Not to get OT, but do you listen to Oceansize as well?

My conky is fairly similar to yours, and in my alignment I have top_middle and I am also using ${alignc) around my two lines. Mine stays centered no matter what.

EDIT: Also just noticed you have a value of 5 for your x gap. Mine is set at 0.

Awesome. That ${alignc} was all I needed. Thanks. And yes, I do listen to Oceansize too.

.conkyrc
```

#avoid flicker                                                
double_buffer yes                                             

#own window to run simultanious 2 or more conkys

own_window_transparent yes

#borders

#shades

#position
gap_x 5  
gap_y 0  
alignment top_center

#behaviour
update_interval 1

#colour

#default_shade_color 000000
own_window_colour 222222   

#font
use_xft yes
xftfont Segoe Semibold:pixelsize=10

#to prevent window from moving
use_spacer none               
minimum_size 1280 0           

#mpd
mpd_host localhost
mpd_port 6600     

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen
#${font Grunge:size=12}${time %a  %b  %d}${alignr -25}${time %k:%M}

#$alignc center text
TEXT
${voffset -1} Cpu: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${cpu}% ${color} Mem: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${mem} ${color}  |  ${color} Uptime: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${uptime_short}${color}  |  ${color} Down: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${downspeed wlan0} Kb/s ${color} ${totaldown wlan0} downloaded${color}  |  Up: ${color} ${color d0d0d0}${upspeed wlan0} Kb/s ${color} ${totalup wlan0} uploaded${color}  |  ${color}Root: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${fs_free /} ${color} Home: ${color d0d0d0}${font}${fs_free /home}${color}  |  Gmail: ${color d0d0d0}${execi 300 python ~/.scripts/gmail.py}${color}  |  Now Playing : ${color d0d0d0}${font}${exec echo `qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player GetMetadata | grep -m1 artist | cut -d : -f 2` " - " `qdbus org.kde.amarok /Player GetMetadata | grep -m1 title | cut -d : -f 2`}${color}

### Post by cardinals_fan on 2008-11-11
> **elmer_42 said:**
> My school also uses a system that posts them online (PowerSchool), but you have to enter a password to get access to your grades. If EGP requires this, could you tell me how you get by this?
Here's the deal: it depends on what happens after the password is entered.  For EGP, it just loads a regular html page with your code at the end.  Check out the attached screenshot.  If I right-click in the report, select "This Frame" (on Firefox), and click the info option, it lists the frame's individual address.  From there on out, it's some easy lynxing and filtering.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-11
> **What is in a name? said:**
> I noticed your pager has the name of each desktop on it. Is that a new feature of Xfce 4.6?

Can't remember, though I suspect it's new as it's buggy; xfconf either doesn't remember workspace names or simply doesn't display them and every time I login, I've got to open up the pager properties to re-tick the checkbox so it displays the names.


I will say one new feature I'm enjoying, though: not only can you click-and-drag task list items around and rearrange them but if you drag one to the pager, you can send it to your desired workspace.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-12
> **andrek said:**
> Speaking about Xfce 4.6.. it seems like it won't have any graphical menu editor. What's more, it's a true pain in the a*s to edit it manually, too.

Once you get your head around it, it's not too bad. Frankly, with their (presumably) complete implementation of the freedesktop.org standards, if they did create a graphical editor, it'd probably be as bad as Gnome's alacarte and the old menu editor was pretty shoddy as well.

### Post by perfectska04 on 2008-11-14
> **wersdaluv said:**
> Wow. It's nice. Why don't you enable it by default? I love your dark gradients. They're consistent up to the GDM themes.

When you force a panel bg, then people start complaining that they can't make their panels transparent or use custom bg's. It's just easier to disable it and leave it available for anyone who wants it.

### Post by andrewabc on 2008-11-16
For people fighting with sonata and mpd, it is technically impossible to get it to work on ubuntu just by installing sonata and mpd.

Here's a short how-to that might help other. The key is to install paprefs, and change sound setting in mpd.conf to prevent errors.

> To get sonata/mpd runing need to install
paprefs

Enable network access to local sound devices
	Don't require authentication

Make sure music_directory is pointing to where music located.

In sonata:
Music directory point to music directory

Then create your database
sudo mpd --create-db

In mpd.conf in audio output area put

audio_output {
type	"pulse"
name	"My MPD Pulseaudio Output
}


I tried getting mpd and sonata working for over a year, tried 3 times. I had to go onto mpd irc channel and spend an hour getting help from someone to figure out why it wasn't working.

I have to agree. I use sonata because my keyboard multimiedia keys work with it (gnome keys). GMPC works as well, you can add hotkeys for it. Also with sonata album art works, in GMPC it does not work (I need to compile a plugin, which I'm not doing).

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-11-17

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-11-19
Just a quick memo: disabling tty's 2 to 6 was probably one of the best moves I ever did in these last months, concerning my PC. My RAM consumption was significantly reduced, the Swap partition is barely being used at all, and everything is running smoother... Ahhhh...


Just though I could share it with y'all.

---

### Post by perfectska04 on 2008-11-19
> **What is in a name? said:**

Just though I could share it with y'all.

I thought disabling the tty's only saved a few hundred KB's of memory. I usually don't bother with them because of that, but I find using preload and a low vm.swappiness to increase overall performance. /offtopic

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-11-19
Perhaps disabling tty's isn't ideal, but heck, with less than 512 MB of RAM... What can a boy do?

Which security concerns should I have?

> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Howto please. I know we're running the same RAM so this would be helpful.

```
cd /etc/event.d
sudo mv tty2 tty2~
sudo mv tty3 tty3~
sudo mv tty4 tty4~
sudo mv tty5 tty5~
sudo mv tty6 tty6~
```

Or just do sudo bash before typing the above commands.
Mileage may vary.

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-11-19
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Perhaps disabling tty's isn't ideal, but heck, with less than 512 MB of RAM... What can a boy do?

Which security concerns should I have?



```
cd /etc/event.d
sudo mv tty2 tty2~
sudo mv tty3 tty3~
sudo mv tty4 tty4~
sudo mv tty5 tty5~
sudo mv tty6 tty6~
```

Or just do sudo bash before typing the above commands.
Mileage may vary.

Technically, the correct way to disable a console tty is to comment out the corresponding entries in /etc/inittab  ;)

### Post by ayoli on 2008-11-19
> **yabbadabbadont said:**

I think that was right before upstart, but may not be the same now.

I ve read about a var ACTIVE_CONSOLES in /etc/default/console-setup where you can set the number of tty and then editing the tty files you don't want (instead of renaming) and commenting the start line.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-19
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Well, I've always made it clear that I'm not that well informed about deeply technical stuff in Linux. That said, which of those two suggestions is the most correct one?
After you first mentioned it last night, I did some googling. I ended up doing the following:

- Set the active consoles variable in the console setup to 1-2.

- Renamed the tty(x) files to disabled_tty(x).

- Opened up each of the disabled_tty(x) files and commented out everything which wasn't already commented out.

After that, it finally worked for me.

Now, for an on-topic tangent: I got sick of looking at the default Gnome icons everytime I ran something as root so I decided to mirror my icon theme over to the root home directory.

[[IMG]http://img510.imageshack.us/img510/2740/iconspn7.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img510.imageshack.us/img510/2740/iconspn7.jpg)[[IMG]http://img510.imageshack.us/images/thpix.gif[/IMG]](http://g.imageshack.us/thpix.php)

I didn't even know you *could* replace the icons within synaptic. Thorough job, WIIAN? Eikon2 must be the most complete icon theme I've ever encountered.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-11-19
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> After you first mentioned it last night, I did some googling. I ended up doing the following:

- Set the active consoles variable in the console setup to 1-2.

- Renamed the tty(x) files to disabled_tty(x).

- Opened up each of the disabled_tty(x) files and commented out everything which wasn't already commented out.

After that, it finally worked for me.

Now, for an on-topic tangent: I got sick of looking at the default Gnome icons everytime I ran something as root so I decided to mirror my icon theme over to the root home directory.

[[IMG]http://img510.imageshack.us/img510/2740/iconspn7.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img510.imageshack.us/img510/2740/iconspn7.jpg)[[IMG]http://img510.imageshack.us/images/thpix.gif[/IMG]](http://g.imageshack.us/thpix.php)

I didn't even know you *could* replace the icons within synaptic. Thorough job, WIIAN? Eikon2 must be the most complete icon theme I've ever encountered.

Thanks for the tips, everybody, I'll reboot in a minute to check it out. Though my first method worked as well, from what I saw.

Icarus, actually I learnt how to change those icons on Synaptic after observing the Meliae theme. Which is how I learn most things... Observing.

<off-topic>Who came up with wide screens, anyway? Why not increase screen height, instead. It's vertical screen space that is often in short supply, not horizontal screen space.</off-topic>

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-19
> Who came up with wide screens, anyway? Why not increase screen height, instead. It's vertical screen space that is often in short supply, not horizontal screen space.16:10 was chosen as a defacto standard for two reasons: Good for working with multimedia (think watching videos or using Photoshop) and it's perfectly shapped for an 'open book' layout (ie two A4 documents side-by-side).

Frankly, I rarely feel short of vertical screen space and I've only got 900 lines of resolution. Even with a 16:10 screen format, I still feel boxed in at the sides, though. It's very difficult to have Firefox open and still have enough usable screen space beside it (considering most web pages expect 1024).

---

### Post by Kosimo on 2008-11-19

<off-topic>Who came up with wide screens, anyway? Why not increase screen height, instead. It's vertical screen space that is often in short supply, not horizontal screen space.</off-topic>

That's exactly why I have a vertical panel (Always with windows list bug of course).
I have much more wide than height space, so, let's use it. My firefox doesn't even have a status bar, and I'm using hidemenu addon, to even increase for some pixels my reading space.

Let's create the vertical panel "two member" club, as looks that anyone else is happy wasting hight pixels on wide screens!

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-11-21
> **GarethMB said:**
> Can you post your details please.

The GTK theme is a custom theme that I am currently working on that is based primarily off of my Murrina Smoothie Blueberry theme.  I'm still working out some kinks.  The all-blueness is starting to annoy me, and I'm thinking of changing it.

The Emerald theme is a blue modification of my Coffee and Cream theme.

The primary font is Sawasdee 9.  It's regular weight on everything but the desktop, where it is bold.

The panel background can be found here:  [https://dl.getdropbox.com/u/29948/w7pb.png](https://dl.getdropbox.com/u/29948/w7pb.png)  (Thanks to Mazza558 for that one)

The icons are from the Eikon theme. Everything but the folder icon is from his newest release.  The folder icons are from an alternate folders folder within release candidate 2.

The Conky configuration can be found on What is in a Name's website.  It's the more recent one.

The RSS scroller is called Snackr.  It requires the Linux version of Adobe Air to run.

The wallpaper is from the Colored Backgrounds pack, which can be found here:  [http://alexander-gg.deviantart.com/art/Colored-Backgrounds-102172919](http://alexander-gg.deviantart.com/art/Colored-Backgrounds-102172919)

Here is a slimmed down version of my previous screenshot.  I removed the Snackr ticker and I made the panel smaller.  I have to admit: working with GTK themes is a lot more fun and a whole lot less frustrating than KDE themes.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-11-21
> **eightmillion said:**
> I've created another new emerald theme, and I'm curious to know what people think.

[[img]http://xs433.xs.to/xs433/08475/newwindec886.png.xs.jpg[/img]](http://xs.to/xs.php?h=xs433&d=08475&f=newwindec886.png)

That is pretty awesome.  It's very strange, because it gives the windows an odd sense of depth that normal Emerald themes don't. 

The only problem I see with it is that the smooth, curved feel of the Emerald theme badly clashes with the hard, square feel of the Skulpture theme.

They really need to make more themes for KDE.  I mean, the primary choices are GTK (which offers a lot of different possibilities, but doesn't always work correctly), QtCurve, Oxygen, and Skulpture.  They don't even have Domino, which is a crying shame.

### Post by ddnev45 on 2008-11-21
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> After you first mentioned it last night, I did some googling. I ended up doing the following:

- Set the active consoles variable in the console setup to 1-2.

- Renamed the tty(x) files to disabled_tty(x).

- Opened up each of the disabled_tty(x) files and commented out everything which wasn't already commented out.

After that, it finally worked for me.

Now, for an on-topic tangent: I got sick of looking at the default Gnome icons everytime I ran something as root so I decided to mirror my icon theme over to the root home directory.

[[IMG]http://img510.imageshack.us/img510/2740/iconspn7.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img510.imageshack.us/img510/2740/iconspn7.jpg)[[IMG]http://img510.imageshack.us/images/thpix.gif[/IMG]](http://g.imageshack.us/thpix.php)

I didn't even know you *could* replace the icons within synaptic. Thorough job, WIIAN? Eikon2 must be the most complete icon theme I've ever encountered.

Can I get link to the owl wallpaper? I queried some of the usual sites and couldn't find this picture.

And off topic; RE new Star Trek, does "looks crap" mean the same in South Australia as it does in SW USA (bad movie)?

### Post by ddnev45 on 2008-11-21
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> 

Edit: Also, need some advice. RSS via conky has proved too limited. How else should I get feeds on my desktop?

Thanks for the picture.

Took a look at your script (in screenshot) file; maybe one too many ${alignr} in the script. I made one change:

code:

this:  sed -e :a -e 's/<[^>]*>/${alignr}/g;/</N' |\
to this: sed -e :a -e 's/<[^>]*>//g;/</N' |\

I know somewhere between zero and zilch about sed, so there may be some syntax errors. Also, on my system, I get those squares at the end of lines when the spacing is off.

Hope that helps.

Ubuntu 8.04, Openbox Murrina334 (modified), tint2, conky, and an owl.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-22
> **eightmillion said:**
> Wow. It's looks like you're trying to see if your display actually can show 16.9 million colors.



Ok, I see what you're trying to do. If you attach all your conky files, I'm sure that I can get that to happen with one conky. By the way, what's the font you're using for you conky.

They're all pretty much the same:

```
background yes

use_xft yes
# xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont LucidaMacBold:size=7
override_utf8_locale yes

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 1

update_interval 1
draw_shades no
draw_outline yes
draw_borders no
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1
default_color BFFFB7 #3FB2C1 #CFE5D3 #BFFFB7 #B1B1B1 #FF8086 #61FFE2 #7EFFF7 #7EB6FF #BAF5FF #BFFFB7 #FFF2E6 #9DFFDD #B599FF 
default_shade_color ffffff
default_outline_color 505050
own_window yes
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
own_window_colour 121212
alignment bottom_left
gap_x 10
gap_y 12
no_buffers yes
uppercase no
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none
minimum_size 150 0
mail_spool $HOME/Maildir/

#${rss http://www.abc.net.au/news/indexes/idx-australia/rss.xml 60 feed_title}

TEXT
${font LucidaGrande:size=10}${color ffffff}ABC News | Australia
${font}${rss http://www.abc.net.au/news/indexes/idx-australia/rss.xml 10 item_titles 5}
``` Think you can infer from that which fonts i'm using, too.

### Post by el mariachi on 2008-11-22
just extract it and copy the resulting folder to ~/.icons 
if you don't have that folder (it's hidden) just create it :D

if you use Gnome you could just drag-and-drop the tar.gz file into the appearance window

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-11-22
**etnlIcarus**:

I figured out a way to show multiple rss feeds side by side. It's just not a very good solution, more like a proof of concept/dirty hack. I modified the conky-rss script to pull in five different feeds and lay them out side by side. Conky then calls the script and redirects output to a file and then reads this line by line. There's some kind of limitation with conky displaying the full output of the script all at once. It only works correctly with a monospaced font. Multiple conkys is an infinitely better solution.

---

### Post by jedimasterk on 2008-11-23
> **grazed said:**
> that's like slapping an Mac OSX wallpaper in there, since it is "Unix-like" as well.

linux isn't unix. =/ out of all the major unix-like OS's (solaris,BSD,OSX,etc.) linux is probably the farthest away.

Wikipedia:
Linux (commonly pronounced IPA: /&#712;l&#618;n&#601;ks/ in English; variants exist[1]) is a generic term commonly used to refer to "Unix-like" computer operating systems which use the Linux kernel.

### Post by andrek on 2008-11-23
> **jordanmthomas said:**
> Yes, they do render them differently.  Ubuntu applies some patches that Arch doesn't.
But you can always use cairo-ubuntu, libxft-ubuntu, fontconfig-ubuntu and freetype2-ubuntu packages from AUR to make them as awesome as the ubuntu ones.

### Post by Killeroid on 2008-11-23
[[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3043/3053944254_93322243a1.jpg[/IMG]](http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3043/3053944254_75c479e8be_o.png)

[[IMG]http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3272/3053115887_1a7694ddfd.jpg[/IMG]](http://farm4.static.flickr.com/3272/3053115887_12093bd44d_o.png)

Using tint for my taskbar and trayer for notification area and gnome-do as my launcher.

GTK & Metacity: **[Dust]("https://code.launchpad.net/dusttheme/0.2/0.2")**
Icons : **[Crashbit]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/CrashBit?content=71140")**
Wallpaper: **[Airborne 2]("http://farm1.static.flickr.com/78/211909545_7a75f67b6c_o.jpg")**
Firefox theme : **[Dustfox]("http://launchpad.net/dusttheme-firefox/trunk/0.1.20090921/+download/dustfox-0.1.20080922.xpi")**
Font: Calibri 8

My tintrc:
```

#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_mode = single_desktop
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom left
panel_size = 1100 26
panel_margin = 0 0
panel_padding = 0 0
font_shadow = 0

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 9
panel_border_width = 2
panel_background_color = #000000 0
panel_border_color = #000000 0

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 1
task_width = 200
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 2
task_icon_size = 0
task_font = Calibri bold 8
task_font_color = #ffffff 59
task_active_font_color = #ffffff 90

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 3
task_background_color = #000000 40
task_active_background_color = #000000 55
task_border_width = 1
task_border_color = #d1d1d1 34
task_active_border_color = #d1d1d1 40

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = Calibri bold 8
time2_format = %A %d %B
time2_font = Calibri bold 6
clock_font_color = #ffffff 90

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = close
mouse_right = none
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify


```

My startup command for trayer:
```

trayer --expand true --transparent true  --alpha 255 --edge bottom --align right --expand true --SetDockType true --widthtype request

```

How do you get conky to output as text to the terminal, rather than just draw to the desktop? I've tried using your conkyrc and piping it to awesome-client like you say but it just draws to the desktop.

Update: I added "out_to_console yes" and it outputs to the console, but for some reason this just doesn't work when piping to awesome-client. I tried running awesome-client and entering the output from conky and it works. Using echo and piping to awesome-client also works, but piping from conky just doesn't work. What am I doing wrong?

Update 2: Found the answer here: [http://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=56859](http://bbs.archlinux.org/viewtopic.php?id=56859)
Had to modify the conky source code.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-11-25
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> While I'm a fan of dark themes, I've always been reluctant to make the colours slightly blue, the reason being it just doesn't seem to work as it should. My humble suggestion would to make the blue even less pronounced.

Well, I started out with a much more vibrant blue, and I found it was very unattractive.  So I took a lot of the saturation out of the blue.  I'm fairly satisfied with the result, except I really need to change the color of the progressbar and scrollbar.  The light gray stands out too much from the rest of the color scheme.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-25
> **What is in a name? said:**
> I can't seem to be satisfied with any panel layout I choose. Though for the moment this one seems to be fine.Just figure out the panel plugins you really *need* and drop the rest. I personally don't find that I need any launchers as the xfce menu is so well designed. I don't need a menu plugin as the desktop provides that. I don't need a, "show desktop", button as my 4th workspace is usually unused.

Aside from being better on memory usage, you've got less clutter and the desktop becomes easier to use when you impose strict rules upon your own usage habits.


Also, am I the only person who doesn't use a graphical login manager? Obviously it may prove difficult if you're using multiple environments but login + starx 4 lyfe.

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-11-28
> **happysmileman said:**
> What distro you use?
And how easy was it to install the Beta?

You can install KDE 4.2 beta on Ubuntu just by adding this to your /etc/apt/source.list:

```
deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/project-neon/ubuntu intrepid main

```

Then do a "sudo aptitude update && sudo aptitude install kde-nightly"
It even installs in /opt/ so it doesn't mess up your current kde4 installation.

> **joebodo said:**
> I need my computer to look just like this. Is there a theme available?

There's not really a theme, but I can link you to everything in the screenshot. First off, it's KDE 4 and compiz. The dock at the bottom is cairo-dock which is available in the repositories.

The wallpaper is available [here]("http://toffeenut.deviantart.com/art/Metal-Lights-Wallpaper-86093066")

The widget style is [bespin.]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Bespin?content=63928")

The icons are [Oxygen Refit 2 Black.]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Oxygen+Refit+Black?content=89298")

Everything else is on my [drop.io]("http://drop.io/downdiagonal")

You need the first five downloads there. dworkindark.colors, dworkindark.emerald, amarok2simple.skz (for the cover art widget), conkys.tar (for the lyrics and clock on the desktop), and font.tar.

Let me know if you need anything else. :)

### Post by dbbolton on 2008-11-28
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> By now there's probably a few MurrinaDark's and MurrinaBlack's. Not to be an ****, myself but people really should go for less generic names when releasing stuff.

And for the record, I searched gnome-look and deviantart for an existing "MurrinaDark" before I released it. There wasn't one.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-11-30
Decided to give Compiz another crack.

[url=http://img227.imageshack.us/img227/1553/compmy5.png][img]http://img149.imageshack.us/img149/6313/compsxk0.png[/img]
http://img227.imageshack.us/img227/1553/compmy5.png[/url]

Bicubic filtering doesn't cause a rendering fallback anymore (no more <1fps effects) but I'm pretty sure that's more progress in the xorg-video-ati driver and mesa, rather than an improvement in Compiz.

Smooth scrolling in mozilla apps is no longer completely retarded and is instead on-par with the slightly retarded lag present in IE and Opera but I'm pretty sure that's got to do with gecko 1.9's improved rendering backend, not compiz.

2D acceleration has improved somewhat (X11 video tolerable) but that's possibly not the result of any improvements in Compiz.

Lack of DRI2 in xserver1.5 means video/3D overlays still misbehave.

Emerald is just as bug-ridden as it was two years ago and less stable (emerald manager locks up every time you use a slider).

Window manager behaviour is annoying (margins? drop-to-bottom-of-stack? disable resize-from-top option?)

Settings manager is still as bewildering as it was a year ago (and possibly moreso with the addition of even more options). Duplicated functionality. Options fully visible - even when they're not available given broader chosen options. Poor basic descriptions. Functionality which seems to stray from any coherent hierarchical categorisation.

So far, it hasn't crashed (which is more than I could say for KDE 4.1 w/o desktop effects) but every now and then, it maxes out my CPU.

Conclusion: Perpetually a tech-demo and still not ready for Joe Shmo. The fact that this is enabled by default on most distros is ...disturbing. I thought only MS hated their users.

/end rant

---

It is enabled by default with minimal effects (and it's easy to desactivate trough apparence dialog) and metacity as WM. I don't find this so disturbing.
